Lewis                \n            \n                                    There's probably a joke to be made about Caspian's new eight-inch single — that the Massachusetts post-rock band's music is too expansive to fit on a traditional seven-inch, so they had to go for a bigger format. The new release, Castles High, Marble Bright, soundtracks a diary-like video of the group's European tour, and serves as a nice complement to last year's full-length Dust and Disquiet. That album found the traditionally instrumental band experimenting with (gasp!) vocals, both as an emotive supplement to their booming crescendos (as on the track \"Echo and Abyss\") and on (double-gasp!) a folksy ballad (\"Run Dry\"). Post-rock may not be quite as en vogue as it was in the Nineties, but Caspian has found ways to evolve its sound, building layers of instruments and melodies that are plenty emotive even without the
